Jamison Brereton

33 (387)
Indra
Saс╣Гvaraс╣Зa Pr─Бj─Бpatya
10 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The structure of this hymn is relatively straightforward. It begins (vs. 1) with the poetтАЩs praise of Indra, presented as an inducement to the god to come to his sacrifice, followed (vss. 2тАУ3) by the usual tropes of a тАЬjourneyтАЭ hymn, includ ing the yoking of IndraтАЩs horses. The poet recognizes that there are competing sacrifices (vs. 4a), but continues to urge Indra to choose to come to his (vs. 5). There follow two verses (6тАУ7) asking for gifts from Indra. The hymn ends with a three-verse d─Бnastuti (8тАУ10), praising the gift of horses from a number of dif ferent patrons.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra Although the general outline of this hymn is pretty straightforward, it is full of interpretational problems and grammatical and syntactic obscurities, and the meter is very messy.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFeeble as I am, I offer praise to the great and vigorous Indra, for this purpose, (that he may grant) strength to (our) people; he who, associated with the Maruts, shows favour to this person n when praised for the sake of sustenance.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Associated with the Maruts: samarya is an epithet of Indra; three explanations are offered for samarya: martyaiс╕е, stotс╣Ыbhiс╕е, sahitaс╕е, together with mortals, that is, with worshippers, yuddham─Бnairmarud─Бdibhiс╕е, with the Maruts and other combatants, or samara arhaс╕е, fir or suited to war

Jamison Brereton

I conjure up a great (praise) for the great, powerful one among superior men, for Indra so very powerfulтАФI who am not so powerfulтАФ
he who, praised among the people as battle-ready, takes note of the good thought (directed) toward him at the prize-winning.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich begins and ends with an etymological figure: #m├бhi mah├й тАж tav├бse ├бtavy─Бn#. The tav├бse also repeats the same form from the preceding p─Бda.

I supply ┼Ыr├бvaс╕е тАШpraiseтАЩ with m├бhi, since this is a frequent collocation. Sim.

Geldner, though K├╝mmel (258) and Witzel Got┼Н take it as adverbial.

With Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н uncertainly) I reluctantly interpr. p─Бda-final nс╣Ы╠Д╠Бn as a gen. pl.

(or standing for a gen. pl.), as is sometimes necessary. Oldenberg interpr. it rather as a dat. pl., which I donтАЩt understand.

With Geldner I construe itth─Б╠Бwith tav├бse; I assume it adds strengthening to that repeated word. K├╝mmel (258) instead takes it as an expression of the method of praise: тАЬauf diese Weise,тАЭ so apparently also Witzel Got┼Н, though muted (тАЬalsoтАЭ).

In the 2nd hemistich the referent of asmai is at issue. The standard view (Geldner, Oldenberg, Witzel Got┼Н) is that it refers to the singer, the тАЬnot so strongтАЭ I. In GeldnerтАЩs interpr. this involves rendering asmai sumat├нm тАж cik├йta as тАЬder тАж diesem (S├дnger) seine Gunst zugedacht hat.тАЭ That sumat├н- could refer to IndraтАЩs benevolence is easy, but тАШzudenkenтАЩ as an interpr. of cik├йta is hard. This pf. stem ordinarily means either тАШtake note ofтАЩ or тАШappear asтАЩ (latter generally middle). Witzel Got┼Н give the pf. its usual meaning but this leaves asmai without much to do in the clause. By contrast, I take Indra as the referent of asmai. It is not rare for enclitic forms of this pronoun to refer to the subject: a reflexive is not necessary. Under this interpr. sumat├н- has its common meaning тАШgood thoughtтАЩ = poem, and Indra takes cognizance of this sumat├н-, which is тАЬfor him.тАЭ Cf. VII.31.10 pr├бcetase pr├б sumat├нс╣Г krс╣З╠е udhvam where the sumat├н- of the poets is intended for a god (Indra, in fact) in the dative who is characterized as pr├б тИЪcit.

Griffith

GREAT praise to Indra, great and strong mid heroes, I ponder thus, the feeble to the Mighty,
Who with his band shows favour to this people, when lauded, in the fight where spoil is gathered.

Geldner

Ein gro├Яes Lied ersinne ich auf den Gro├Яen, Starken unter den M├дnnern, auf Indra, ich der Schw├дchere, auf den so Starken, der vor allem Volke gepriesen im Wettbewerb umworben bei der Lohngewinnung diesem S├дnger seine Gunst zugedacht hat.

Grassmann

Dem grossen, starken Indra leg’ ans Herz ich die M├дnner recht, dem starken ich, der schwache, Der kriegerisch, gepriesen bei dem Volke, im Kampfe Huld erwiesen diesem Manne.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Indra, meditating upon us, fasten the traces of yourborses, (incited), showerer (of benefits), by those praises in which you have suitable delight, and do you therefore overcome (for us) hostile men.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Indra, being conjured up by our chants, have fixed the yoking thong for the fallow bays, you bull.
You will drive here just so, following your pleasure, bounteous one. You will bring (good things); you will be victorious over the peoples of the stranger.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The (pseudo-)participle dhiyas─Бn├б- clearly patterns with d─лdhi ye in 1a, hence my complementary тАШbeing conjured upтАЩ. I take it to mean that IndraтАЩs epiphany at the sacrifice is brought about by our chants (arka├нс╕е), that his appearance there is literally тАЬthought upтАЭ by our thoughts. This notion is close to what is found in the previous hymn V.32.11 (at least by my interpr.), that every sacrifice brings a тАЬnewest Indra,тАЭ that the Indra of the sacrificial epiphany is newly created by sacrificial activity every time. The standard interpr. of dhiyas─Бn├б- by Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н] is more pedestrian: Indra becomes attentive (тАЬaufmerksam gewordenтАЭ) through our hymns. The other occurrence of the stem, in X.32.1, in my opinion fits my interpr., but to be honest neither passage is absolutely clear. As for the stem itself, dhiyas─Бn├б- does not pattern with the majority of -as─Бn├б- stems discussed ad IV.3.6, and I do not have a satisfactory account of it.

The s├б tv├бm phrase does not conform to my rules for the use of s├б with 2nd ps.

reference (see my тАЬS├б fig├йтАЭ), and I likewise canтАЩt account for it.

The y─Б╠Б(с╕е) beginning the 2nd hemistich is problematic. If it is a rel. prn. it has to be a fem. pl., and there is no obvious referent in the context (h├бr─лс╣З─Бm in b belonging to a masc. stem h├бri-). Therefore with Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) and, very cautiously, Oldenberg, I take it as a verb form, belonging to тИЪy─Б тАШdriveтАЩ. (Note the past part. y─Бt─Б╠Бс╕е in 5b.) Because it is followed by two subjunctives, v├бkс╣гaс╕е and sakс╣гi (the latter a тАЬsiimperativeтАЭ derived from a subjunctive), I take y─Б╠Б(с╕е) as subjunctive as well. Indeed, if it is read y─Бah, the extra syllable would fix the meter of this p─Бda – but since the hymn is full of metrical disturbances, this is not a strong argument. Neither Geldner nor Witzel Got┼Н indicates how they interpr. the morphology, but both tr. as an imperative, as they do the two following verbs.

Both Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н take ary├бс╕е and j├бn─Бn as parallel acc. pl., while I make ary├бс╕е a gen. sg. dependent on j├бn─Бn. There is no way to tell; Thieme (Fremdl., 11 n. 2) refuses to deal with the passage at all.

Griffith

So made attentive by our hymns, Steer! Indra! thou fastenedst the girth of thy Bay Coursers,
Which, Maghavan, at thy will thou drivest hither. With these subdue for us the men who hate us.

Durch unsere Preislieder aufmerksam geworden, hast du nun, o Bulle Indra, deinen Falben den Strang angelegt. Komm hierher, du Freigebiger, nach deinem Wohlgefallen; fahre her, werde mit den vornehmen Nebenbuhlern, den anderen Leuten fertig!

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╣реЗ рдЛрд╖реНрд╡ рдорд╣рдиреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдпрддреН рдпреЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреН рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреНрддрдГ рддреНрд╡рджреНрднрдХреНрддреЗрднреНрдпреЛрд╜рдиреНрдпреЗ ‘рдЕрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рд╕рдГ рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рдЕрд╕рдВрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ рдЕрд╕рдиреН рдЖрд╕рдиреН рдЕрднрд╡рдиреН рдЕрдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорддрд╛ ред рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рдкрд░рд┐рд╡реГрдврдВ рдХрд░реНрдо ред рддрджреНрд░рд╣рд┐рддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рддреЗ рдирд░рд╛рдГ рддреЗ рддреНрд╡рджреАрдпрд╛рдГ рди рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЕрддрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреНрдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН рдЕрднрд┐ рдЖрдЧрдиреНрддреБрдВ рддрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдВ рд░рдердордзрд┐ рддрд┐рд╖реНрда ред рд╣реЗ рд╡рдЬреНрд░рд╣рд╕реНрдд рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рджреЗрд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рд╢реНрд╡рдГ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдпрдВ рд░рдердорд╛рд░реЛрдвреБрдВ рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рдВ рдкреНрд░рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдореН рдЖ рдпрдорд╕реЗ рдирд┐рдпрдордпрд╕рд┐ рддрдордзрд┐ рддрд┐рд╖реНрда рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSince, mighty Indra, those who, differing from us, and not united with you through their lack of devotion, are not yours; therefore, divine holder of of the thunderbolt, who are possessed of excellent horses, ascend the car, whose reins you guide, (to come to our sacrifice).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These (horses) of yours (will) not (remain) unyoked because of us [i.e., because of our failure], lofty Indra, if itтАЩs for lack of a (yoking)
formulation.
Mount on the chariot with mace in hand. You with the good horses will hold your own rein, o god.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The sense of the first hemistich – that by reciting the (yoking-)formulation we will do our part to ensure that your (IndraтАЩs) horses will be yoked – is fairly clear, but the syntax is messy. First, itтАЩs couched as a triple negative construction: тАЬit is not that X will not happen because of not-Y,тАЭ which already puts it on the edge of parsability. The parsing problem is slightly increased by the fact that the content of the negative тАЬthatтАЭ clause is expressed through a periphrasis involving a negated participle+copula (├бyukt─Бsaс╕е тАж ├бsan тАЬwill be/remain unyokedтАЭ). Then, the position of y├бd is utterly non-standard, being found deep in the clause, after several different constituents, right before the final word. I tried various ways to produce a conforming subordinate clause from the text, but failed. The published translation тАЬif it’s for lack of a (yoking) formulationтАЭ (as if abrahm├бt─Б y├бd were a separate embedded clausette) gives the appearance of (almost) succeeding, but it doesnтАЩt accurately represent the text (though I still think it might represent the purport of this odd word order). A more accurate tr. would be тАЬSince these horses тАж. because of a lack тАж,тАЭ as the dependent clause for the main clause in cd. I remain disturbed by the structure of this dep. cl. A separate problem is the abh├н asm├бd in p─Бda a. The abh├н is stranded in the middle of the p─Бda (though immed. after the caesura) and in any case has no verb from which it could have been separated in tmesis. In the absence of anything else to do with it, the default option seems to be to construe it with asm├бd, and this phrase has long (see OldenbergтАЩs reff.) been compared to I.139.8 asm├бd abh├н, likewise in the middle of the p─Бda though in opposite order. The problem is that abh├н as a preposition seems otherwise only to take the acc. Nonetheless, connecting the two seems the best bet, with a meaning such as тАЬwith regard to usтАЭ or, better reflecting the ablative, my тАЬbecause of us.тАЭ So Oldenberg, Witzel Got┼Н. Cf. also Humbach et al. (G─Бth─БsтАж and the Other Oldenberg Avestan Texts, II.118), ad Y 35.5 (Yasna Hapta┼Лhaiti) ahmaс╣н hiiaс╣н aib─л, a phrase meaning (in his view) тАЬwhich is with us,тАЭ with which he compares both our passage and I.139.8. However, Narten (YH, 271-72), fld. by Hinze (Zoroastrian Liturgy, 77-78), interprets this three-word phrase, occurring twice in the YH (Y 35.5, 40.1), as containing a postposition aib─л governing the neut. acc. hiiaс╣н not the abl.

ahmaс╣н, with the whole meaning тАЬfrom us towards which,тАЭ thus тАЬas far as we are concernedтАЭ (Hintze, 78).

They were not turned to us-wtrd, lofty Indra! while yet through lack of prayer they stood unharnessed.

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреЗ рддрд╡ рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рднреВрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдкреБрд░реВ рдкреБрд░реВрдгрд┐ рдмрд╣реВрдирд┐ ред рдЙрдХреНрдерд╛ рдЙрдХреНрдерд╛рдирд┐ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджрд╛ рдЙрд░реНрд╡рд░рд╛рд╕реБ рд╕рд╕реНрдпреЛрдкреЗрддрд╛рд╕реБ рднреВрдорд┐рд╖реБ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрднреВрддрд╛рд╕реБ рдЧрд╡реЗ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпреБрджрдХрд╛рдп рдпреБрдзреНрдпрдиреН рдЬрд▓рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдмрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рдиреН рд╕рдВрд╣рд░рдиреН рдЪрдХрд░реНрде рдХрд░реЛрд╖рд┐ рднреЗрджрдирдореН ред рдХреБрддреНрд░реЗрддрд┐ ред рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдп рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрд╡реЗ рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпреЗ рдУрдХрд╕рд┐ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ ред рд╡реГрд╖рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛ рд╕рдиреН рддрддрдХреНрд╖реЗ рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрдпрд╕рд┐ ред рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ рджрд╛рд╕рд╕реНрдп рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдмрдиреНрдзрдХрд░реНрддреБрд░реЗрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдордХрд╕реНрдп рдЕрд╕реБрд░рд╕реНрдп рдирд╛рдо рдЪрд┐рддреН рдирд╛рдорд╛рдкрд┐ рддрддрдХреНрд╖реЗ рдирд╛рд╢рдпрд╕реАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInasmuch, Indra, as many praises are yours, therefore, combating for the sake of (shedding) water on fertile (lands), you have effected (the discomfiture of its obstructors); you, who are the showerer (of benefits), have on behalf of the sun, destroyed in his own dwelling the very name of (the asura), D─Бsa, in battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just as there are many hymns that exist for you, Indra, and many are (the deeds) you have done for the cow, when fighting over the
meadows,
(and many [the paths]?) you carved out also for the sun in your [/his] own home, as bull you (have carved out) even the names of the D─Бsa in the contests.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another troubled vs., though the first hemistich is more transparent than the second. The first thing to notice is that the accent on cak├бrtha in b indicates that b must still be under the domain of y├бd in p─Бda a, as parallel dependent clauses. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) attempt to make initial pur┼л╠Бa single-word main clause on which they both depend (тАЬViel ist, was тАжтАЭ). This assumes that pur┼л╠Бis a neut. sg. here. Although the existence of a neut. sg. in -┼л is standard doctrine (see Lanman, Noun Inflec., 406-7, AiG III.145, etc.), this grammatical truism rests primarily on GrassmannтАЩs identification of twelve forms of pur┼л╠Бas sg. (see Lanman and AiG), but in only one instance, the late X.94.5, does this seem the likely interpr. (There is also one form of ur┼л╠Бand, for Lanmann, two of m├нth┼л, which is better taken as an adv.) I do not therefore think that

-┼л is a possible neut. sg. ending, except, perhaps, in X.94.5. Here the most obvious way to construe pur┼л╠Бis with p─Бda-final neut. pl. ukth─Б╠Б, the subject of s├бnti. The attempt to impose a singular interpr. on pur┼л╠Б, as antecedent for the following relative clause with plural subject, yields the awkward rendering of Geldner: тАЬViel ist, was deine Preislieder sindтАЭ with mismatch of number (Witzel Got┼Н more elaborate, but not less clumsy).

For b the only adjustment is to carry pur┼л╠Бover from p─Бda a and supply a term like kс╣Ыt─Б╠Бс╣Зi or k├бrm─Бс╣Зi, easily generated from cak├бrtha: тАЬmany are (the deeds) you have done тАжтАЭ The 2nd hemistich is more problematic. The first question is how to relate p─Бda c and d. Geldner takes them as parallel independent clauses with the same verb tatakс╣г├й, while Witzel Got┼Н takes it as a single cl. (also K├╝mmel 207). With Geldner I take them as two clauses and agree that they share a verb, but think that c is a dependent clause still under the control of y├бd in p─Бda a and parallel to ab, with d the main clause resuming them all.

A related issue is the apparent change of person from 2nd sg. address to Indra in ab and (supposed) 3rd sg. reference to him in cd. The only evidence for this 3rd ps.

reference is the verb tatakс╣г├й, which is one of only two medial forms of this pf. in the RV. It has no obvious medial value here, and in fact the presence of a dat. of benefit (s┼л╠Бry─Бya) eliminates one possible way of accounting for the middle form. (K├╝mmel [207] suggests a тАЬBedeutungskomponenteтАЭ тАШ(auch) in seinem eigenen InteresseтАЩ, which seems a bit desperate.) The puzzle of the middle is somewhat reduced if we interpret the form as second sg. mid. The presumed preform *tatakс╣г-с╣г├й would surely come out as our tatakс╣г├й, and it would make sense to substitute this nonce middle form for the non-transparent active 2nd sg., which should be *tat├бkс╣г-tha ├а *tataktha – whereas the active 3rd sg. tat├бkс╣гa is non-problematic and indeed well attested. So the supposed change of person and the middle form can be accounted for by the same explanation.

After confronting these formal issues, there remains the very knotty problem of what the hemistich is expressing, and part of this depends on whether the relations between Indra and S┼лrya here are friendly or hostile: elsewhere they are sometimes one, sometimes the other. (Here I think they are friendly.) A syntactic questions is whether n─Б╠Бma is the only object of tatakс╣г├й or if the clause in c (if it is a separate clause) has a different object. Geldner opts for the former choice, I for the latter, and I also think that the verb is used in different senses in c and d, positive in c, negative in d.

In c I supply pur┼л╠Бagain from a and tentatively supply тАШpathsтАЩ as the object, bringing to mind the various passages in which a god (usually Varuс╣Зa) makes or digs out paths for the sun to follow through the sky – e.g., I.24.8 ur├║с╣Г h├н r─Б╠Бj─Б v├бruс╣Зa┼Ы cak─Б╠Бra, s┼л╠Бry─Бya p├бnth─Бm ├бnvetav─Б╠Бu, VII.87.1 r├бdat path├│ v├бruс╣Зo s┼л╠Бry─Бya. In one late passage (X.111.3) it is Indra who is named as pathikс╣Ы╠Бt s┼л╠Бry─Бya тАЬpathmaker for the sun.тАЭ ItтАЩs also worth noting that, leaving aside this one, 5 of the other 10 occurrences of the dat. s┼л╠Бry─Бya occur in a path-making context. Though, admittedly, I have no parallels using the root тИЪtakс╣г тАШfashion, carveтАЩ, it seems in the right general semantic range. As for ├│kasi sv├й this can refer either to IndraтАЩs or to S┼лryaтАЩs тАЬown home,тАЭ since both of them inhabit the same celestial realms; I favor the SunтАЩs.

As for d, as is recognized by all, the similarly phrased X.23.2 ├бva kс╣гnaumi d─Б╠Бsasya n─Б╠Бma cit must be compared. In that passage Indra says тАЬI whet down even the name of the barbarian,тАЭ in my tr. Though this passage is the obvious comparandum, it is hardly transparent in itself or in its bearing on our passage, and in fact I think the two passages are less close semantically than their joint isolation invites us to think. In X.23.2 Indra seems to be boasting about his victory over the D─Бsa, which is so complete that even his name is obliterated or at least violently ground down. But тИЪtakс╣г generally refers to creating something by carving off bits or fashioning in some other way. Perhaps here it means that Indra, just by fighting (and presumably defeating) the D─Бsa, has still made the latterтАЩs name conspicuous, as if by carving it into a surface. (Or perhaps, closer to X.23.2, Indra has obliterated the D─БsaтАЩs name as if by gouging it out of a surface.) But either of these interpr. raises a crucial question: what would it mean literally to carve a name into (or gouge it out of) a surface before the existence of writing?! In any case I think that the contrastive positive/negative use of тИЪtakс╣г in c and d makes the verb sit uneasily in both and poses special challenges to the audience to decode the metaphor in each p─Бda.

As should be obvious, I do not consider my interpr. of this vs. or most of its part settled and sure. I also donтАЩt understand the sequence of ideas. As indicated in the published introduction, I think that the first p─Бda, positing many hymns for Indra, may refer to the existence of competing (─Аrya) sacrifices. The second p─Бda cites his activities as a warrior on earth; the dat. тАЬfor the cowтАЭ may either mean that Indra has fought in order to obtain cows (for the ─Аrya warriors he is fighting beside) or that he has won meadows for (the ─АryasтАЩ) cows to graze in – in either case advancing the ─Аrya cause.

In contrast c sets out his beneficial cosmic activity – keeping the sun on track (if my interpr. of the details of the p─Бda is correct), which in turn is beneficial to mankind.

In at least the first two cases I think thereтАЩs an implicit ─Аrya presence, which contrasts with the explicit D─Бsa in d.

Griffith

Thou, because many lauds are thine, O Indra, wast active warring in the fields
for cattle.
For Surya in his own abode thou, Hero, formedst in fights even a Dasa’s nature.

Geldner

Viel ist, was deine Preislieder sind, o Indra, was du f├╝r die Kuh getan hast, um die Fluren k├дmpfend. Er beschnitt sogar der Sonne ihren Namen im eigenen Hause, in den K├дmpfen beschnitt der Bulle auch des Dasa Namen.

Grassmann

Wenn viele Spr├╝che, Indra, dir geweiht sind, so wirkst f├╝r Heerden du um Fluren k├дmpfend; Der Held erreichte k├дmpfend die D├дmonen im eignen Hause, zu der Sonne Bestem.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe, Indra, are yours, and yours are they who are the leaders (of rites), promoters of (your) strength, and willing applicants (to you); all-powerful Indra, may adherents worthy of commendation and faithful, come to us, like Bhaga, in battles.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

All-powerful Indra: ahi┼Ыuс╣гma is an epithet of Indra, sarvato vy─Бptabala, of all-pervading strength; like Bhaga in battles: satv─Б bhago na havyaс╕е prabhс╣Ыtheс╣гu c─Бruс╕е: prabhс╣Ыta = war or sacrifice; hence, may a faithful folloer or ally, sarva bhс╣Ыty─Бdiс╕е, come, like Bhaga, as an associate, c─Бru saс╣Еgant─Б, tobe commanded, havya, in sacrifices, or defied, pratibhaс╣нair─Бhv─Бtavya, in battles; as the divine Bhaga comes as our ally, so may followers and others come

Jamison Brereton

We are yours, IndraтАФas are the superior men born as a troop
[=Maruts?] and the driving-chariots.
As a consummate warrior he [=Indra] should come here to us, o you with the serpentтАЩs hissтАФdear, like Bhaga to be invoked at our forays [/dear like a portion to be offered at our (ritual) presentations].

Jamison Brereton Notes

What constitutes the predicate in ab is disputed. Flg. Oldenberg and the model of VII.30.4, I take ab as constituting an тАЬX and which YтАЭ construction, with doubled тАЬand which YтАЭ (more accurately schematized as тАЬX and which Y and (which) ZтАЭ).

The predication is simply te тАЬof you, yours,тАЭ an assertion of possession. It is predicated of us (vay├бm t├й) as well as тАЬwhich menтАЭ (y├й ca n├бraс╕е) and тАЬ(which) chariotsтАЭ (тАж ca r├бth─Бс╕е) – literally тАЬwe and which men and (which) chariots are yours.тАЭ Both of the latter two are further characterized in b, the men by a participial phrase (┼Ы├бrdho jaj├▒─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬhaving been born as a troopтАЭ), the chariots by a simple participle (y─Бt─Б╠Бс╕е тАШdriven, drivingтАЩ). Witzel Got┼Н seem to follow this interpr. as well, though with some filigree in the middle that seems over-elaborate. Klein (DGRV I.49 n. 10) sets out the schema as above and tr. sim. (I.196). Geldner by contrast takes the predication to be ┼Ы├бrdho jaj├▒─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е, applied to both us and the men, with the chariots left hanging: essentially тАЬwe and the man are born as your troop, and the chariots.тАЭ Besides the syntactic isolation of the chariots in GeldnerтАЩs rendering, it also unduly extends the reference of ┼Ы├бrdho jaj├▒─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е. The тАЬmenтАЭ of p─Бda a must be, as often, the Maruts, and it is only they who тАЬhave been born as a troop,тАЭ not also us. The word gaс╣З├б- is almost exclusive to the Maruts, and the birth of the Maruts is a common topic (e.g., I.64.2, 4).

The phrase r├бtho n├б y─Бt├бс╕е appears in I.141.8. See comm. there, where I suggest that a y─Бt├б- r├бtha- is a particular kind of chariot, perhaps one meant for long journeys, rather than referring to the current state of motion of any specific chariot(s).

The problem with p─Бda c is the clash between the voc. ahi┼Ыuс╣гma and the 3rd sg.

verb jagamy─Бt with its nom. subj. s├бtv─Б. The stem s├бtvan- in the sg. is almost always used of Indra, and in this context – a hymn dedicated to Indra and both praising his powers and begging him to deploy them on our behalf – it is difficult to imagine that we would then express a wish that some indefinite or at least unidentified warrior should come our way instead (as in GeldnerтАЩs тАЬUns m├╢ge тАж ein Krieger kommenтАЭ; Witzel Got┼Н almost identical). Surely Indra is the warrior we want! This would require a shift from 2nd to 3rd ps. ref. between ab and cd, but this is not problematic. What is problematic is the voc., which should also refer to Indra. Grassmann solves this by positing a bahuvr. ahi┼Ыuс╣гma-s├бtvan- тАШwhose warriors have a serpentтАЩs hissтАЩ (тАШdessen Helden wie Schlangen zischenтАЩ). Unfortunately the accent is definitively against this interpr.

I have no neat solution, but am firm in my belief that the s├бtv─Б is Indra. For a similar vocative/nominative cross, see vasav─Бnaс╕е in the next vs. (6a); these two problems may be connected.

I take the simile in d as an elaborate pun, playing on the double sense of the three members, bh├бga-, h├бvya-, and prabhс╣Ыth├б-. The first can be both the name of the god Fortune and a common noun тАШportionтАЩ; h├бvya- can belong to тИЪh┼л, hv─Б тАШcallтАЩ or тИЪhu тАШpour, offerтАЩ; pra тИЪbhс╣Ы can refer either to the presentation of arms (and the carrying off of booty) in a hostile situation or to the presentation of offerings at a sacrifice. Cf. the double sense of pr├б тИЪbhс╣Ы in nearby V.32.4-5, 7 and comm. there.

The first meanings just given for the three items coalesce into one simile, the second ones in another.

Dein sind wir, dein die Schar-gebornen M├дnner, die Maruts, dein die Wagen, die da fahren, Mit Helden komm er, die wie Schlangen zischen, zu uns, wie Bhaga lieb, zum Mahl geladen.

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдкрдкреГрдХреНрд╖реЗрдгреНрдпрдВ рд╕рдВрдкрд░реНрдХрд╛рд░реНрд╣рдВ рдкреВрдЬреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдУрдЬрдГ рдмрд▓рдВ рддреНрд╡реЗ рд╣рд┐ рддреНрд╡рдпрд┐ рдЦрд▓реБред рддреНрд╡рджрдзреАрдирдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдиреГрддрдорд╛рдирдГ рдиреГрддреНрдпрдиреН рдЕрдорд░реНрддрдГ рдЕрдорд░рдгрдзрд░реНрдорд╛ рд╕рдГ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡рд╕рд╡рд╛рдирдГ рдЖрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рджрдпрдиреН рд╕реНрд╡рддреЗрдЬрд╕рд╛ рдЬрдЧрддреН рдиреГрдореНрдгрд╛рдирд┐ рдиреГрдордгрд╛рдирд┐ рджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рдгрд╛рдирд┐ ред рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрд░рдпреНрдпрдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рдпрд╛ рдЪрд╢рдмреНрджрдГ ред рдПрдиреАрдореН рдПрддрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдВ рд╢реНрд╡реЗрддрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдВ рд░рдпрд┐рдВ рдзрдирдВ рджрд╛рдГ рджреЗрд╣рд┐ ред рдЕрд╣рдВ рдЪ рдЕрд░реНрдпрдГ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╕реНрдп рддреБрд╡рд┐рдордШрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрдзрдирд╕реНрдп рдЪ рджрд╛рдирдВ рдкреНрд░ рд╕реНрддреБрд╖реЗ рд╕реНрддреМрдорд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGlorious, Indra, is your strength, exulting, immortal, and clothing (the world with light); do you give us riches, and brilliant wealth, and I will greatly praise the munificence of the opulent lord.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Exulting: nс╣Ыtam─Бna = liс╣н, dancing, nс╣Ыtyam; brilliant wealth: en─лm

Rayim = liс╣н, white riches, perhaps a reference to silver

Jamison Brereton

For, Indra, in you are strength to be nurtured and manly powers. As prancing immortal,
give us dappled wealth, you winner of goods. I will start up the praise for the gift of the powerfully bounteous stranger.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first question about this vs. is the structure of the first hemistich. The standard interpr. (Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н, also Oldenberg, Klein [DGRV I.263-64]; see also Kulikov -yapres., 580) takes the two p─Бdas as separate clauses with ca conjoining them. There are several problems with this division: 1) ca is not comfortably at home as clauseconjoiner and usually conjoins NPs; 2) with nс╣Ыmс╣З─Б╠Бni in the domain of the 2nd clause, it must be the obj. of the participle (or pseudo-participle; see below) nс╣Ыt├бm─Бnaс╕е, but non-causative forms of тИЪnс╣Ыt тАШdanceтАЩ are never transitive. Both difficulties disappear if we take nс╣Ыmс╣З─Б╠Бni ca as conjoined with immediately preceding ├│jaс╕е as joint subject of the first clause in the hemistich (so also Lowe, 251; see below). The phonological play between nс╣Ыmс╣З─Б╠Бni and nс╣Ыt├бm─Бс╣Зaс╕е may account for the postponing of nс╣Ыmс╣З─Б╠Бni till the second p─Бda, inserting a p─Бda break between the two conjoined nouns. This phonologically driven positioning may also help account for the very late positon of h├н. The loc. prn. tv├й ordinarily takes initial position in its clause/verse line, and h├н would be expected to follow in WackernagelтАЩs position. But the whole structure may have been shifted rightwards to allow nс╣Ыmс╣З─Б╠Бni to neighbor nс╣Ыt├бm─Бс╣Зaс╕е.

nс╣Ыt├бm─Бс╣Зa- presents difficulties of its own, even after its supposed object has been eliminated. This participle is the only occurrence of the supposed them. aor. (or 6th cl. pres.) in all of Sanskrit. Although, since all forms of this root are poorly attested in the RV, this is not necessarily problematic on its own, the -ya-present (1x in RV) does continue post-RV (see Kulikov, Vedic -ya-presents, 578-80), and moreover all other verb forms to this root in Vedic are active. Lowe (Participles in Rigvedic Sanskrit, 250-51) suggests that it is an artificial form based on the wellattested splv. nс╣Ы╠Бtama- тАШmost manly, most heroicтАЩ. This is an attractive hypothesis – among other things, Indra is frequently called nс╣Ы╠Бtama-; the word regularly appears in immediate post-caesura position, as nс╣Ыt├бm─Бс╣Зaс╕е does here; and it would be playing not merely phonologically but also etymologically with nс╣Ыmс╣З─Б╠Бni. Lowe (p. 152) tr.

тАЬbeing the most heroic,тАЭ reflecting its nonce jury-rigged participial form. I do think, however, that the form also consciously references тИЪnс╣Ыt тАШdanceтАЩ. Indra is regularly called a nс╣Ыt├║- тАШdancer, prancerтАЩ, and note the pun involving nс╣Ы╠Б- тАШmanтАЩ in VI.63.5 n├бr─Б nс╣Ыt┼л (of the A┼Ыvins). I would therefore modify the published translation to тАЬAs the most manly [/ the prancing] immortal тАжтАЭ In c ray├нm must be fem., as occasionally elsewhere, given the fem. adj. ├йn─лm. The stem v├бsav─Бna- тАШpossessing goods, winning goodsтАЩ (?) is attested 5x, once as an unaccented voc. sg. vasav─Бna (X.22.15), otherwise accented and with orthodox -a-stem forms, incl. nom. sg. v├бsav─Бnaс╕е (I.174.1). The form here looks of course like a nom. sg. but lacks accent. Grassmann calls it тАЬf├дlschlich unbetontтАЭ; Lubotsky gives it an accent and a rightward star (v├бsav─Бno*). This seems the best course; I think an attempt to assign it to different stem (perhaps an aberrant -as stem) is too elaborate, esp. in this hymn with numerous тАЬoffтАЭ forms: see esp. the voc. ahi┼Ыuс╣гma for expected nom. in 5c. The published translation pays more attention to the lack of accent and tr. as voc.; it would be equally possible to weigh the nom. sg. ending more heavily and tr. it as an appositive subject: тАЬas winner of goods, give us dappled wealth.тАЭ Despite the tr.

тАЬwinner of goods,тАЭ I do not think the stem contains a form of тИЪvan but is rather a pseudo-participle (another one, but athematic) built to v├бsu- тАШgood(s)тАЩ. Elsewhere I render it тАШgoods-lordтАЩ and the like.

In d pr├б тАж stuс╣гe d─Б╠Бnam тАЬI will start up the praise for the giftтАЭ is an analytic expansion of the noun d─Бnastuti, which, however, is not attested in Vedic or, it seems, anywhere else in Sanskrit lit., though the term is in common use in Vedic scholarship.

The last three (or possibly four) vss. in this hymn constitute such a d─Бnastuti, and the poet seems to signalling that it is coming up. In the published translation I identify the ar├нtuvimagh├б- as Indra; I now would be more circumspect, since I now think the phrase applies both to Indra and to the patrons praised in vss. (7 or) 8-10. See also ary├бс╕е in 9d.

Griffith

Strength much to be desired is in thee, Indra: the Immortal dances forth his hero exploits.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHero, Indra, with your protection defend us, praising and worshipping (you), and be propitiated (by drinking) of the well-effused and agreeable Soma juice that yields (a defensive) covering in combat.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

So, help us, Indra, with your help. Protect the singers, the bards, o champion.
And please those giving the skin of the dear, well-pressed honey at the winning of prizes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. provides a transition between the praise-hymn proper and the d─Бnastuti. On the one hand, it straightforwardly makes requests of Indra, as hymnfinal vss. tend to do, and it begins with ev─Б╠Б, a frequent introducer of the final summary vs., but it also turns its attention in cd to those who facilitate the sacrifice, i.e., the patrons. The participle d├бdataс╕е тАШgivingтАЩ that characterizes them is telling. Geldner suggests that the d─Бnastuti begins with 7c and notes that like 7c the vss. of the d─Бnastuti begin with ut├б.

The meter of the first hemistich is badly mangled. Oldenberg blames the poet тАЬdessen Formgef├╝hl unzweifelhaft schwach war.тАЭ But it may be a good strategy to mark the new section with a metrical jolt. Curiously the vs. is mostly free of the verbal knots that bedevil the earlier parts of the hymn.

Geldner suggests plausibly that the тАЬskin of the honeyтАЭ is the skin on which the soma is prepared.

Griffith

Thus favour us, O Indra, with ihy succour; Hero, protect the bards who sing thy praises.
Be friendly in the fray to those who offer the skin of beautiful and well-pressed Soma.

Geldner

So begnade uns, Indra, mit deinen Gnaden; sch├╝tze, du Held, die lobsingenden Dichter, und stelle die zufrieden, die bei der Auslohnung das Fell des wohlgepre├Яten, willkommenen S├╝├Яtrankes verschenken.

Grassmann

So hilf uns denn mit deinen H├╝lfen, Indra, und sch├╝tz, o Held, die Dichter, die dich preisen; Geniess vom lieben, s├╝ssen, sch├╢ngebrauten dess, der beim Mahl den Somaschlauch dir brachte.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay those ten bright homes, the tift to me of the pious gold-possessing Trasadasyu, the son of Purukutsa, of the raceof Girikс╣гita, convey me (to the sacrifice) and may I proceed quickly with the rites.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And these gold-bedecked (horses) of my patron, Paurukutsya
Trasadasyu, when they are givenтАФ
let his ten white ones convey me. I am attended by the intentions of Gairikс╣гita.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is unclear whether the horses in ab and those in c are the same or different.

In the published translation they are treated as the same; the standard tr. take them as separate groups. The two occurrences of m─Б (a, c) may support the standard view, in which case vahantu needs to be supplied in the first hemistich (so Geldner, etc.). I take sa┼Ыce in pass. sense: тАЬI am followed/accompanied.тАЭ Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н, also Klein I.425) take it to mean тАЬbe in agreement with,тАЭ but I do not know of other occurrences of тИЪsac with this meaning. (GeldnerтАЩs overelaborate set of explanatory glosses in n. 8d and n. 2 to that n. may attest to his discomfort with it.) The тАШintentionsтАЭ by which I am attended are GтАЩs intentions to give; see the expansion on kr├бtu- in 9b. I think the point is not that the poet thinks itтАЩs a good idea for G. to give horses to him (that is, agrees with G), but that GтАЩs intentions to give are the poetтАЩs escorts, as it were. (One is reminded of the curious beings known as r─Бtiс╣г─Б╠Бc- тАШGiftescortтАЩ.) Indeed these тАЬintentionsтАЭ may be the actual horses given; see 9b where the тАЬbountiesтАЭ produced by such intention are also actualized as horses.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As just noted, 7c begins with ut├б as do vss. 8-10, but those vss. of the d─Бnastuti proper are further unified, all beginning ut├б ty├й m─Б.

Griffith

And these ten steeds which Trasadasyu gives me, the goldrich chief, the son of Purukutsa,
Resplendent in their brightness shall convey me. Gairiksita willed it and so came I hither.

Geldner

Und mich sollen diese von dem freigebigen Patron Trasadasyu, dem Purukutsasohn geschenkten goldgeschm├╝ckten Rosse fahren; es sollen mich seine zehn Rotschimmel fahren. Ich stimme mit den Absichten des Gairiksita ├╝berein.

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOr may those bay, well-actioned horses, the donation of Vidhata, the son of Maruta┼Ыva, (convey me); or (may) the thousands (of treasure) which he was bestowing upon and giving to me, entitled to respect, and the ornaments which he presented (to decorate) the person n, (contribute to the ceremony).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bestowing upon and giving to me: cyavatana dad─Бna causing to alight upon, giving

Jamison Brereton

And (let) these (convey me)тАФthe ruddy (horses) of M─Бrut─Б┼Ыva, the bounty of his intentions at the giving of the distribution,
(when) Cyavat─Бna was giving a thousand of his own to me. Afterward (the singer) sang as if to marvel (at the gift) of the stranger [=Indra].

Jamison Brereton Notes

In p─Бda a the published translation reads тАЬAnd (let) these (convey me)тАЭ; the тАЬmeтАЭ should not be in parens.

The bahuvr─лhi kr├бtv─Бmagha- is curiously formed, with instr. kr├бtv─Б as its first member, and the published translation тАЬthe bounty of his intentionsтАЭ oversimplifies its structure in order to avoid impossibly awkward English: a full tr. of b would be тАЬ(the horses displaying/constituting) the bounty (produced) by his intention at the time of giving in[/of] the ceremony.тАЭ In other words, the horses that the poet receives possess (that is, embody) M─Бrut─Б┼ЫvaтАЩs bounty effected by his intention (to give). See 8d.

Geldner takes vid├бthasya as a PN, the patron whose patronymic is M─Бrut─Б┼Ыva, and Mayrhofer (PN s.v.) seems to agree. But there seems no reason not to interpr. it as an example of the well-attested common noun тАШceremony (of distribution)тАЩ, esp. since it fits this context so well. Witzel Got┼Н do not follow Geldner

The part. d├бd─Бnaс╕е appears to be the predicate of this clause. Though rare, med. forms of тИЪd─Б without ─Б╠Бseem to mean тАШgive of oneself / oneтАЩs own goodsтАЩ. See also IX.52.3.

I donтАЩt entirely understand d. ─Бn┼лk├бm is a hapax, but I follow Oldenberg in taking it as an adverbial meaning something like тАШafterwardsтАЩ; so apparently also Witzel Got┼Н. Geldner, fld.

by Klein (I.425), takes it as the obj. of ─Бrcat, as тАШlast (song)тАЩ. See GeldnerтАЩs n. 9d.

The standard interpr. (Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н], Oldenberg, Klein I.425) take ary├бс╕е as nom. sg., referring to Cyavat─Бna of c, and Thieme (Fremdl. 85) also thinks itтАЩs probably nom. sg., but declines to discuss the passage because of the obscurity of ─Бn┼лk├бm. But a patron like Cyavat─Бna should not be chanting or singing; that is the province of the poet-priests he is patronizing. Moreover, ary├бс╕е echoes gen. sg. ary├бс╕е in 6d, which announced the d─Бnastuti to come, and I think the form should be interpr. in the same way in the absence of evidence to the contrary. In 9d I think that the gift of the ar├н- is still in question (as in 6d). The unnamed poet praised (тАШsangтАЩ ─Бrcat) his gift for the wonder (v├бpuс╣гe) of it – of its over-the-top munificence.

English translation:

тАЬOr may the bright and active steeds bestowed upon me by dhvanya, the son of Lakс╣гmaс╣Зa (bear me); the riches endowed with greatness, that have been presented, have passed (to the dwellings) of the с╣Ъс╣гi Saс╣Гvaraс╣Зa, like cows to their stallс╣гтАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And (let) these (convey me)тАФthe enjoyable (horses) of Dhvanya Lakс╣гmaс╣Зya, the very bright ones having being marshaled.
Through the greatness of his wealth the proffered (horses) have come, like cows to the cowpen, (to the enclosure) of the seer Saс╣Гvaraс╣Зa.

As in 9a тАЬmeтАЭ should be removed from parens.

The notion of enclosure in cd puns on the name of the Poet Saс╣Гvaraс╣Зa тАШentirely enclosingтАЩ vel sim.

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)
  • рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░:
  • рд╕рдВрд╡рд░рдгрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдкрддреНрдпрдГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ (рдзреНрд╡рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рдзреНрд╡рдирд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдХреБрд╢рд▓ рдФрд░ (рд╕рдВрд╡рд░рдгрд╕реНрдп) рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рд░рд╛рдпрдГ) рдзрди рдХреЗ (рдорд╣реНрдирд╛) рдорд╣рддреНрддреНрд╡ рд╕реЗ (рдЙрдд) рдФрд░ (рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдордгреНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди (рдЛрд╖реЗрдГ) рдордиреНрддреНрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдЬрд╛рдирдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХреЗ рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдз рдореЗрдВ (рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд╛рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдЬрди рд╣реИрдВ (рддреНрдпреЗ) рд╡реЗ (рдЧрд╛рд╡рдГ) рдЧреМрд╡реЗрдВ (рд╡реНрд░рдЬрдореН) рдЧреЛрд╖реНрда рдХреЛ (рди) рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рдЕрдкрд┐) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдд (рдЧреНрдордиреН) рдЬрд╛рддреА рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдорд╣рддреНрддреНрд╡ рд╕реЗ (рдорд╛) рдореБрдЭ рдХреЛ рднреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рдФрд░ рдЬреЛ (рдпрддрд╛рдирд╛рдГ) рдпрддреНрди рдХрд░рддреА рд╣реБрдИ (рд╕реБрд░реБрдЪрдГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░реАрддрд┐рд╡рд╛рд▓реА рдореБрдЭ рдХреЛ (рдЬреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрдирддрд╛рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реИрдВ, рдЙрдирдХреЛ рд╕рдм рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИ ред рдЬреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрди рд╕реЗ рдирд╣реАрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдП рдХреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдП рдХреА рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдмрдЫреЬреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЧреМрд╡реЗрдВ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдзрди рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реерезрежрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рддреЗрдВрддреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдп рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЗ рдзреНрд╡рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрд╡рд░рдгрд╕реНрдп рд░рд╛рдпреЛ рдорд╣реНрдиреЛрдд рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдордгреНрдпрд╕реНрдпрд░реНрд╖реЗрдГ рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрдпреЗ рдЧрд╛рд╡реЛ рд╡реНрд░рдЬрдиреНрдирд╛рдкрд┐ рдЧреНрдордиреН рддрдерд╛ рдорд╣реНрдирд╛ рдорд╛ рдорд╛рдордкрд┐ рдЧреНрдордиреНред рдпрд╛ рдпрддрд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╕реБрд░реБрдЪреЛ рдорд╛ рдЬреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддреБ реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЙрдд) (рддреНрдпреЗ) (рдорд╛) рдорд╛рдореН (рдзреНрд╡рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рдзреНрд╡рдирд┐рд╖реБ рдХреБрд╢рд▓рд╕реНрдп (рдЬреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдГ) рдкреНрд░реАрддрд╛рдГ (рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдордгреНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рд╕реБрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгреЗрд╖реБ рднрд╡рд╕реНрдп (рд╕реБрд░реБрдЪрдГ) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрдкреНрд░реАрддрд┐рдорддреНрдпрдГ (рдпрддрд╛рдирд╛рдГ) (рдорд╣реНрдирд╛) рдорд╣рддреНрддреНрд╡реЗрди (рд░рд╛рдпрдГ) рдзрдирд╕реНрдп (рд╕рдВрд╡рд░рдгрд╕реНрдп) рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХреГрддрд╕реНрдп (рдЛрд╖реЗрдГ) рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд┐рджрдГ (рд╡реНрд░рдЬрдореН) рд╡реНрд░рдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдЧрд╛рд╡рдГ) рдзреЗрдирд╡рдГ (рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд╛рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдпрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ (рдЕрдкрд┐) (рдЧреНрдордиреН) рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдпреЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрдиреЗрдирд╛рд╜рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рдВ рд▓рдмреНрдзрд╕реНрдп рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╡рддреНрд╕рд╛рдиреН рдЧрд╛рд╡ рдЗрд╡ рдзрдирдорд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ реерезрежрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпреЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬреА рдорд╛рдгрд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрдирдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ рдЕрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреАрдЪреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреА рд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХреЗрд▓реЗрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдЪреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд. рд╡рд╛рд╕рд░реВ рдЬрд╕реЗ рдЧрд╛рдИрд▓рд╛ рднреЗрдЯрддреЗ рддрд╕реЗ рддреЗ рдзрди рдорд┐рд│рд╡рд┐рддрд╛рдд. рее резреж рее
